<plain_text><page sequence="1">INDEXES TO THE RECORDS OF THEAUCKLAND INSTITUTE AND MUSEUM VOLUMES 1-33, 1930-1996 L. Furey and B.J. Gill Abstract. General, author and new taxa indexes are presented for the papers in the 57 issues of the Records of the Auckland Institute and Museum published between 1930 and 1996 (volumes 1-33). These issues contain 441 papers and short notes, representing the work of a total of 143 authors and co-authors. Most papers (48%) deal with zoology, especially the taxonomy of gastropod molluscs. The next largest group of papers covers archaeology/ethnology (28%), followed by botany (16%) and geology/palaeontology (7%). As a contribution to the task of documenting New Zealand's biodiversity, the Records contain descriptions of 680 new taxa (including 614 species and subspecies, 63 genera and subgenera and 3 taxa at the family level). KEYWORDS: Index, bibliography, author, new taxa, publication, history, Auckland Museum. INTRODUCTION The four main museums of New Zealand - in Auckland, Wellington, Christchurch and Dunedin - have each attempted to publish scholarly periodicals containing the results of research by their curatorial staff and others. Canterbury Museum (Christchurch) published the first issue of the Records of the Canterbury Museum in 1907, but publication since then has been irregular. The Museum of New Zealand (Wellington; formerly "Dominion Museum" and "National Museum") began publication of a Records , containing several short papers to a volume, in 1942, although various bulletins and monographs were published earlier (Yaldwyn 1982). Otago Museum (Dunedin) has published erratically starting with Records of the Otago Museum - Anthropology in 1964. Auckland Museum was founded in 1852 (Powell et al. 1967) and the Records of the Auckland Institute and Museum was first published on 30 June 1930. The museum's annual report for 1930-31 (Anon. 1931) states: "The Council having authorised the issue of the "Records of the Auckland Institute and Museum," the first number appeared in June. Besides forming a means of publication of the results of research carried out by the staff, the "Records" has already brought us in exchange many valuable overseas publications." Before 1930, museum staff and members of the Auckland Institute and Museum (the Auckland branch of the New Zealand Institute, now the Royal Society of New Zealand) were expected to publish in the Transactions of the New Zealand Institute . Cheeseman (1917), writing of the achievements of the Auckland Institute and Museum on its 50th anniversary, wrote that "the contributions made by its members to the "Transactions of the New Zealand Institute", or independently published, are well and favourably known". The frequency of publication of the Records of the Auckland Institute and Museum has been once annually. An issue has appeared in (or for) every year since 1930, excepting six years (1940, 1943, 1945, 1955, 1963 and 1966; see Table 1). In the earlier years, six issues Ree. Auckland Inst. The Records to date contain 441 papers and short notes by a total of 143 authors and co- authors. The papers deal mainly with life science, earth science and anthropology (Table 2), reflecting the research interests of successive museum staff and of outside researchers who have used the Auckland Museum collections. The Records papers naturally have a bias towards studies relating to the northern half of the North Island. Particular research interests can be traced through the Records. For instance, Auckland Museum has had a long association with field research on the Three Kings Islands, with 47 papers by staff and other professionals on the natural history, geology, ethnology and archaeology of this group. The Records have been a particularly valuable outlet for papers in archaeology, with numerous data-rich descriptive papers on Maori artefact collections, excavation reports and landscape archaeology for which there are few other suitable vehicles of publication. Through the initial co-ordination of Janet Davidson, a former museum archaeologist, there have been numerous papers published in the Records on the archaeology of Motutapu Island and the Coromandel Peninsula. The earlier Records volumes tended to have many short papers, whereas in more recent years there has been a trend towards fewer, longer papers. The Records has published various papers arising from university theses, especially in archaeology and zoology, where research was carried out on museum collections. We believe that the Records papers represent a remarkable contribution to the dissemination of research results in New Zealand given the museum's small staff and</page><page sequence="4">6 FUREY &amp; GILL Table 2. Publication even continued during many of the war years though several staff were on active service. Little research was done during the early war years as staff were concentrating on packing and dispersing the collections for safe-keeping (Anon. 1942: 14-15). ORGANISATION OF THE INDEX This index to the contents of the Records of the Auckland Institute and Museum comprises three separate indexes. First, an index to authors (Index 1). This is ordered alphabetically by the author's or co-author's surname, and the full title of each paper is given as well as the year of publication, issue and pagination. Co-authors are cross-referenced to principal authors. The title is as cited at the head of the paper where there is a discrepancy between this and the entry in the issue's contents page. In some cases the use of colons and commas has been standardised. The year (for all indexes) is the year of publication rather than the nominal year (see Table 1). Second, an index to new taxa (Index 2). This lists alphabetically each new taxon name whether a specific (or subspecific) epithet, a generic (or subgeneric) name or a name at the family (or subfamily) level. This is followed by the rest of the binomen or trinomen (as appropriate), the major group to which the taxon belongs, the author, the year, the issue number, and the page number on which the description of the new taxon begins.</page><page sequence="6">8 FUREY &amp; GILL Last, a general subject-index (Index 3). This contains references for all papers, whether dealing with natural science or human history. As a finding aid, regional geographic headings are included in addition to the specific localities referred to in papers. Archaeological sites are referenced according to the site name and in broad regional groups. Maori names are used (e.g. kumete, pounamu) although there is also a cross-reference under the English equivalent (e.g. bowl, greenstone). Latin names of plants and animals are generally listed as the generic name only. Full binomials are given where there was substantial information about a particular species, a species was cited in the paper's title, or it was the first New Zealand record for that species. NEW TAXA The new taxa described in the Records papers (Index 2) are of special importance because they represent the museum's contribution to the task of cataloguing New Zealand's biodiversity. New taxa described in the Records to date number 680 in total, comprising 535 species, 79 subspecies, 46 genera, 17 subgenera, one family and two subfamilies. The rate of description of new taxa has declined steadily with time (Fig. 1). The 1930s and 1940s saw much descriptive biology. Since then Records papers have increasingly dealt with ecological and other aspects of species already described. Table 3 shows the taxonomie spread of new taxa. Nearly all are animals. Almost 70% of new taxa are gastropods and 9% are bivalves, reflecting the work of the museum's malacologist A.W.B. Powell, and his successor W.O. Černohorsky. The next most numerous group is hexapods (insects and collembolans; 16%). LISTS OF TYPE SPECIMENS The Records contain the following nine lists of type specimens in the Auckland Museum collections: Plants - Cooper 1949b 3(6):397-402. Pteridophytes and Gymnosperms - Goulding 1978 15:37-44. Monocotyledons except Grasses - Goulding 1980 16:87-104. Grasses - Wright 1978 15:45-53. Dicotyledons - Herrick &amp; Cameron 1995 31:89-173. Animals - Powell 1941a 2(5):239-59; Powell 1949d 3(6):403-9. Terrestrial and Freshwater Protists, Annelids and Arthropods - Early &amp; Gilbert 1993 30:49-86. Amphibians, Reptiles, Birds and Mammals - Gill 1983 20:203-15. The first such list (Powell 1941a) arose from the need to pack collections for dispersal during the war (Anon. 1941: 10).</page><page sequence="7">INDEXES 9 EDITORS The editor during the initial years of the Records is not recorded. It was probably G.E. Archey, who was in charge of the museum from 1924 to 1964, and who pursued research in zoology and ethnology. A.W.B. Powell (1901-1987) was editor for volumes 3(4&amp;5) to 6(3), i.e. 1948-1967. He was succeeded by Dr R.C. Cooper, the museum's botanist (assisted by K.A.J. Wise, the museum's entomologist), for volume 6(4-6), i.e. 1969. Then K.A.J. Wise was editor for volumes 7 to 27, i.e. 1970-1990. From volume 28 (1991) to the present, the co- editors have been B.J. Gill, the museum's ornithologist, and N.J. Prickett, the museum's archaeologist. For many years Keith Wise was assisted by an Editorial Committee whose main members were Prof. R.C. Green (Anthropology), Prof. F.J. Newhook (Botany) and Assoc. -Prof. J. Robb (Zoology). Since 1991 the referees have been specialists selected individually for each paper. TECHNICAL Volumes 1-6 were printed at a trim size of 6 by 9.5 inches (150 x 240 mm). This was changed to the present size of 7 by 9.5 inches (180 x 240 mm) from volume 7. Volume 6(3) and earlier issues were printed on matt paper that could not take halftones - halftones were printed as plates on glossy unnumbered pages inserted at the end, and/or within, the part. From volume 6(4-6) glossy paper was used throughout and segregated halftone plates were no longer necessary. The last issue printed by the letterpress process was volume 15 (1978), after which photo-offset was used. Volume 2(2) published in 1937 contained a coloured plate illustrating nudibranch molluscs painted by Powell and printed from "four colour process blocks" donated by Mr G.C. Malcolm. Most of the issues from 1930 to the 1980s were printed by Unity Press Ltd. of Auckland. Other printers have included Auckland Star Commercial Printers, Institute Press (Auckland) and Uniprint (Auckland). MUSEUM BULLETINS In addition to the Records , Auckland Museum has also published, at irregular intervals, a companion periodical entitled the Bulletin of the Auckland Institute and Museum. This has catered for monographic studies too large for inclusion in the Records. Each volume has comprised a single work, or an edited collection of papers on a single topic (Appendix 1). Volume 1 was published in 1941, and the most recent issue was volume 17 (1996). The volumes of the Bulletin have not been indexed. Acknowledgements. The compilation and printing of this index were made possible by a grant from the New Zealand Lottery Grants Board (Environment and Heritage Committee). We thank Ewen Cameron, John Early, Rosemary Gilbert, Jim Goulstone, Margaret Morley, Nigel Prickett and Keith Wise for checking various sections of the indexes.
